      <p>
       The
       <b>
        Dominican Republic
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         República Dominicana
        </span>
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">
         [reˈpuβliˌka ðoˌminiˈkana]
        </a>
       </span>
       ) is a
       <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">
        sovereign state
       </a>
       located in the island of
       <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">
        Hispaniola
       </a>
       , in the
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Antilles" title="Greater Antilles">
        Greater Antilles
       </a>
       archipelago of the
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">
        Caribbean
       </a>
       region. It occupies the eastern five-eighths of the island, which it shares with the nation of
       <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">
        Haiti
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       making Hispaniola one of two Caribbean islands, along with
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin" title="Saint Martin">
        Saint Martin
       </a>
       , that are shared by two countries. The Dominican Republic is the second-largest Caribbean nation by area (after
       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
        Cuba
       </a>
       ) at 48,445 square kilometers (18,705 sq mi), and third by population with approximately 10 million people, of which approximately three million live in the metropolitan area of Santo Domingo, the capital city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-conapofa_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-conapofa-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
        Christopher Columbus
       </a>
       landed on the island on December 5, 1492, which the native
       <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">
        Taíno
       </a>
       people had inhabited since the 7th century. The
       <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Santo_Domingo" title="Captaincy General of Santo Domingo">
        colony of Santo Domingo
       </a>
       became the site of the first permanent
       <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">
        European settlement
       </a>
       in the Americas, the oldest continuously inhabited city, and the first seat of the Spanish colonial rule in the
       <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">
        New World
       </a>
       . After more than three hundred years of Spanish rule the Dominican people declared independence in November 1821. The leader of the independence movement
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_N%C3%BA%C3%B1ez_de_C%C3%A1ceres" title="José Núñez de Cáceres">
        José Núñez de Cáceres
       </a>
       , intended the Dominican nation to unite with the country of
       <a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">
        Gran Colombia
       </a>
       , but no longer under Spain's custody the newly independent Dominicans were forcefully annexed by Haiti in February 1822. Independence came 22 years later after victory in the
       <a href="/wiki/Dominican_War_of_Independence" title="Dominican War of Independence">
        Dominican War of Independence
       </a>
       in 1844. Over the next 72 years the Dominican Republic experienced mostly
       <a href="/wiki/Civil_war" title="Civil war">
        internal conflicts
       </a>
       and a brief return to colonial status before permanently ousting Spanish rule during the
       <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Restoration_War" title="Dominican Restoration War">
        Dominican War of Restoration
       </a>
       of 1865.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_occupation_of_the_Dominican_Republic_(1916%E2%80%9324)" title="United States occupation of the Dominican Republic (1916–24)">
        United States occupation
       </a>
       lasted eight years between 1916 and 1924, and a subsequent calm and prosperous six-year period under
       <a href="/wiki/Horacio_V%C3%A1squez" title="Horacio Vásquez">
        Horacio Vásquez Lajara
       </a>
       was followed by the dictatorship of
       <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Trujillo" title="Rafael Trujillo">
        Rafael Leónidas Trujillo
       </a>
       until 1961. A civil war in 1965, the country's last, was ended by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_occupation_of_the_Dominican_Republic_(1965%E2%80%9366)" title="United States occupation of the Dominican Republic (1965–66)">
        U.S. military occupation
       </a>
       and was followed by the authoritarian rule of
       <a href="/wiki/Joaqu%C3%ADn_Balaguer" title="Joaquín Balaguer">
        Joaquín Balaguer
       </a>
       , 1966–1978. Since then, the Dominican Republic has moved toward
       <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">
        representative democracy
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIADemo_6-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIADemo-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and has been led by
       <a href="/wiki/Leonel_Fern%C3%A1ndez" title="Leonel Fernández">
        Leonel Fernández
       </a>
       for most of the time since 1996.
       <a href="/wiki/Danilo_Medina" title="Danilo Medina">
        Danilo Medina
       </a>
       , the Dominican Republic's current president, succeeded Fernandez in 2012, winning 51% of the electoral vote over his opponent ex-president
       <a href="/wiki/Hip%C3%B3lito_Mej%C3%ADa" title="Hipólito Mejía">
        Hipólito Mejía
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Dominican Republic has the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Latin_American_and_Caribbean_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of Latin American and Caribbean countries by GDP (PPP)">
        ninth-largest economy in Latin America
       </a>
       and is the largest economy in the Caribbean and Central American region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gdp_rank_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-gdp_rank-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Over the last two decades, the Dominican Republic has had one of the fastest-growing economies in the Americas – with an average
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_real_GDP_growth_rate" title="List of countries by real GDP growth rate">
        real GDP growth rate
       </a>
       of 5.4% between 1992 and 2014.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       GDP growth in 2014 and 2015 reached 7.3 and 7.0%, respectively, the highest in the Western Hemisphere.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_22-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the first half of 2016 the Dominican economy grew 7.4% continuing its trend of rapid
       <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">
        economic growth
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_23-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:1-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Recent growth has been driven by construction, manufacturing, tourism, and mining. The country is the site of the second largest
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gold_mine" title="Gold mine">
        gold mine
       </a>
       in the world, the
       <a href="/wiki/Pueblo_Viejo_mine" title="Pueblo Viejo mine">
        Pueblo Viejo mine
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Private consumption has been strong, as a result of low inflation (under 1% on average in 2015), job creation, as well as high level of
       <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">
        remittances
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The Dominican Republic is the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Tourism_rankings" title="World Tourism rankings">
        most visited destination
       </a>
       in the Caribbean. The year-round golf courses are major attractions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-consulate_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-consulate-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A geographically diverse nation, the Dominican Republic is home to both the Caribbean's tallest mountain peak,
       <a href="/wiki/Pico_Duarte" title="Pico Duarte">
        Pico Duarte
       </a>
       , and the Caribbean's largest lake and point of lowest elevation,
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Enriquillo" title="Lake Enriquillo">
        Lake Enriquillo
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The island has an average temperature of 26 °C (78.8 °F) and great climatic and biological diversity.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-consulate_26-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-consulate-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The country is also the site of the first cathedral, castle, monastery, and fortress built in the Americas, located in Santo Domingo's
       <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_Colonial_(Santo_Domingo)" title="Ciudad Colonial (Santo Domingo)">
        Colonial Zone
       </a>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">
        World Heritage Site
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Music and sport are of great importance in the Dominican culture, with
       <a href="/wiki/Merengue_music" title="Merengue music">
        Merengue
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Bachata_(music)" title="Bachata (music)">
        Bachata
       </a>
       as the national dance and music, and
       <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">
        baseball
       </a>
       as the favorite sport.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-embassy_3-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-embassy-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Names_and_etymology">
        Names and etymology
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       For most of its history, up until independence, the country was known as
       <b>
        <i>
         <span lang="es">
          Santo Domingo
         </span>
        </i>
       </b>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firstcolony_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-firstcolony-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       —the name of its present capital and patron saint,
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Dominic" title="Saint Dominic">
        Saint Dominic
       </a>
       —and continued to be commonly known as such in English until the early 20th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The residents were called
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         Dominicanos
        </span>
       </i>
       (Dominicans), which is the adjective form of "Domingo", and the revolutionaries named their newly independent country
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         La República Dominicana
        </span>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In the national anthem of the Dominican Republic (
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Himno_Nacional_Dominicano" title="Himno Nacional Dominicano">
          Himno Nacional
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ) the term "Dominican" does not appear. The author of its lyrics,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emilio_Prud%27Homme" title="Emilio Prud'Homme">
        Emilio Prud'Homme
       </a>
       , consistently uses the poetic term
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Quisqueyano&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Quisqueyano (page does not exist)">
          Quisqueyanos
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , that is, "Quisqueyans". The word "Quisqueya" derives from a native tongue of the Taino Indians and means "Mother of all Lands". It is often used in songs as another name for the country. The name of the country is often shortened to "the D.R."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kraft_32-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Kraft-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Dominican_Republic" title="History of the Dominican Republic">
        History of the Dominican Republic
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-European_history">
        Pre-European history
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Chiefdoms_of_Hispaniola" title="Chiefdoms of Hispaniola">
        Chiefdoms of Hispaniola
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1171" data-file-width="2341" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png/350px-Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png/525px-Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png/700px-Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png 2x" width="350"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The five caciquedoms of Hispaniola
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:El_Pomier_-_Cueva_numero_uno.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/49/El_Pomier_-_Cueva_numero_uno.JPG/250px-El_Pomier_-_Cueva_numero_uno.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/49/El_Pomier_-_Cueva_numero_uno.JPG/375px-El_Pomier_-_Cueva_numero_uno.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/49/El_Pomier_-_Cueva_numero_uno.JPG/500px-El_Pomier_-_Cueva_numero_uno.JPG 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:El_Pomier_-_Cueva_numero_uno.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Pomier Caves are a series of 55 caves located north of San Cristobal in the Dominican Republic. They contain the largest collection of 2,000-year-old rock art in the Caribbean.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Arawakan_languages" title="Arawakan languages">
        Arawakan-speaking
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">
        Taíno
       </a>
       moved into Hispaniola from the north east region of what is now known as South America, displacing earlier inhabitants,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LunaC_33-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-LunaC-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       c. AD 650. They engaged in farming and fishing
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_34-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Encarta-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and hunting and gathering.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LunaC_33-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-LunaC-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The fierce
       <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" title="Island Caribs">
        Caribs
       </a>
       drove the Taíno to the northeastern Caribbean during much of the 15th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The estimates of Hispaniola's population in 1492 vary widely, including one hundred thousand,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-transat_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-transat-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       three hundred thousand,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LunaC_33-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-LunaC-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and four hundred thousand to two million.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Determining precisely how many people lived on the island in
       <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era" title="Pre-Columbian era">
        pre-Columbian times
       </a>
       is next to impossible, as no accurate records exist.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By 1492 the island was divided into five Taíno chiefdoms.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Taíno name for the entire island was either
       <i>
        Ayiti
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        Quisqueya
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anghiera_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-anghiera-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Spaniards arrived in 1492. After initially friendly relationships, the Taínos resisted the conquest, led by the female Chief
       <a href="/wiki/Anacaona" title="Anacaona">
        Anacaona
       </a>
       of Xaragua and her ex-husband Chief Caonabo of Maguana, as well as Chiefs
       <a href="/wiki/Guacanagar%C3%ADx" title="Guacanagaríx">
        Guacanagaríx
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Guam%C3%A1" title="Guamá">
        Guamá
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hatuey" title="Hatuey">
        Hatuey
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Enriquillo" title="Enriquillo">
        Enriquillo
       </a>
       . The latter's successes gained his people an autonomous enclave for a time on the island. Within a few years after 1492 the population of Taínos had declined drastically, due to
       <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">
        smallpox
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       measles, and other diseases that arrived with the Europeans,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_43-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-history-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and from other causes discussed below.
      </p>
      <p>
       The first recorded smallpox outbreak in the Americas occurred on Hispaniola in 1507.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_43-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-history-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The last record of pure Taínos in the country was from 1864. Still, Taíno biological heritage survived to an important extent, due to intermixing. Census records from 1514 reveal that 40% of Spanish men in Santo Domingo were married to Taino women,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and some present-day Dominicans have Taíno ancestry.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guitar_45-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Guitar-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martinez_46-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Martinez-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Remnants of the Taino culture include their cave paintings,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as well as pottery designs which are still used in the small artisan village of Higüerito,
       <a href="/wiki/Moca,_Dominican_Republic" title="Moca, Dominican Republic">
        Moca
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="European_colonization">
        European colonization
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Landing_of_Columbus_(2).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1971" data-file-width="3000" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg/220px-Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg/330px-Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg/440px-Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Landing_of_Columbus_(2).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Christopher Columbus arrives in the New World.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
        Christopher Columbus
       </a>
       arrived on the island in December 5, 1492, during the first of his
       <a href="/wiki/Voyages_of_Christopher_Columbus" title="Voyages of Christopher Columbus">
        four voyages
       </a>
       to the Americas. He claimed the land for Spain and named it
       <i>
        La Española
       </i>
       due to its diverse climate and terrain which reminded him of the
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spanish landscape
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Traveling further east Columbus came across the
       <a href="/wiki/Yaque_del_Norte_River" title="Yaque del Norte River">
        Yaque del Norte River
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Cibao" title="Cibao">
        Cibao
       </a>
       region, which he named Rio de Oro after discovering
       <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">
        gold
       </a>
       deposits nearby.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ferdinand_50-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ferdinand-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On Columbus' return during his second voyage he established the settlement of
       <a href="/wiki/La_Isabela" title="La Isabela">
        La Isabela
       </a>
       in what is now
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Plata_province" title="Puerto Plata province">
        Puerto Plata
       </a>
       on Jan. 1494, while he sent
       <a href="/wiki/Alonso_de_Ojeda" title="Alonso de Ojeda">
        Alonso de Ojeda
       </a>
       to search for gold in the region.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1496
       <a href="/wiki/Bartholomew_Columbus" title="Bartholomew Columbus">
        Bartholomew Columbus
       </a>
       , Christopher's brother, built the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">
        Santo Domingo
       </a>
       , Western Europe's first permanent settlement in the "
       <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">
        New World
       </a>
       ." The colony thus became the springboard for the further Spanish conquest of America and for decades the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Captaincy_general_of_santo_domingo" title="Captaincy general of santo domingo">
        headquarters
       </a>
       of Spanish colonial power in the hemisphere. Soon after the largest discovery of gold in the island was made in the
       <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central,_Dominican_Republic" title="Cordillera Central, Dominican Republic">
        cordillera central
       </a>
       region, which led to a mining boom. By 1501, Columbus' cousin Giovanni Columbus, had also discovered gold near Buenaventura, the deposits were later known as Minas Nuevas. Two major mining areas resulted, one along
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Cristobal,_Dominican_Republic" title="San Cristobal, Dominican Republic">
        San Cristobal
       </a>
       -Buenaventura, and another in Cibao within the
       <a href="/wiki/La_Vega,_Dominican_Republic" title="La Vega, Dominican Republic">
        La Vega
       </a>
       -Cotuy-
       <a href="/wiki/Bonao" title="Bonao">
        Bonao
       </a>
       triangle, while
       <a href="/wiki/Santiago_de_los_Caballeros" title="Santiago de los Caballeros">
        Santiago de los Caballeros
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/La_Vega,_Dominican_Republic" title="La Vega, Dominican Republic">
        Concepcion
       </a>
       , and Bonao became mining towns. The
       <a href="/wiki/Gold_rush" title="Gold rush">
        gold rush
       </a>
       of 1500–1508 ensued.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Floyd_51-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Floyd-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II_of_Aragon" title="Ferdinand II of Aragon">
        Ferdinand II of Aragon
       </a>
       "ordered gold from the richest mines reserved for the Crown." Thus, Ovando expropriated the gold mines of Miguel Diaz and Francisco de Garay in 1504, as pit mines became royal mines, though
       <a href="/wiki/Placer_mining" title="Placer mining">
        placers
       </a>
       were open to private prospectors. Furthermore, Ferdinand wanted the "best Indians" working his royal mines, and kept 967 in the San Cristobal mining area supervised by salaried miners.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Floyd_51-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Floyd-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         68,71,78,125–127
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Under
       <a href="/wiki/Nicol%C3%A1s_de_Ovando_y_C%C3%A1ceres" title="Nicolás de Ovando y Cáceres">
        Nicolás de Ovando y Cáceres
       </a>
       ' governorship, the Indians were made to work in the gold mines, "where they were grossly overworked, mistreated, and underfed," according to Pons. By 1503, the Spanish Crown legalized the distribution of Indians to work the mines as part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Encomienda" title="Encomienda">
        encomienda
       </a>
       system. According to Pons, "Once the Indians entered the mines, hunger and disease literally wiped them out." By 1508 the Indian population of about 400,000 was reduced to 60,000, and by 1514, only 26,334 remained. About half were located in the mining towns of Concepcion, Santiago, Santo Domingo, and Buenaventura. The
       <a href="/wiki/Repartimiento" title="Repartimiento">
        repartimiento
       </a>
       of 1514 accelerated emigration of the Spanish colonists, coupled with the exhaustion of the mines. In 1516, a smallpox epidemic killed an additional 8,000, of the remaining 11,000 Indians, in one month. By 1519, according to Pons, "Both the gold economy and the Indian population became extinct at the same time."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pons_52-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Pons-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Floyd_51-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Floyd-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         191–192
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alcazar_de_Colon.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1152" data-file-width="1728" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Alcazar_de_Colon.jpg/300px-Alcazar_de_Colon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Alcazar_de_Colon.jpg/450px-Alcazar_de_Colon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Alcazar_de_Colon.jpg/600px-Alcazar_de_Colon.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alcazar_de_Colon.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Alc%C3%A1zar_de_Col%C3%B3n" title="Alcázar de Colón">
          Alcázar of Colón
         </a>
         , located in Santo Domingo, is the oldest
         <a href="/wiki/Viceroy" title="Viceroy">
          Viceregal
         </a>
         residence in all of the Americas. It was built for and used by Diego Columbus and his descendents. Diego was the firstborn son of Chistopher Columbus.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       After its conquest of the
       <a href="/wiki/Aztec" title="Aztec">
        Aztecs
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">
        Incas
       </a>
       , Spain neglected its Caribbean holdings. English and French
       <a href="/wiki/Buccaneer" title="Buccaneer">
        buccaneers
       </a>
       settled in northwestern Hispaniola coast and, after years of struggles with the French, Spain ceded the western coast of the island to France with the 1697
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Ryswick" title="Treaty of Ryswick">
        Treaty of Ryswick
       </a>
       , whilst the Central Plateau remained under Spanish domain. France created a wealthy colony Saint-Domingue there, while the Spanish colony suffered an economic decline.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-google48_53-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-google48-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The colony of Santo Domingo saw a spectacular population increase during the 17th century, as it rose from some 6,000 in 1637 to about 91,272 in 1750. Of this number approximately 38,272 were white landowners, 38,000 were free mixed people of color, and some 15,000 were slaves. This contrasted sharply with the population of the French colony of Saint-Domingue (present day Haiti) – which had a population that was 90% enslaved and overall seven times as numerous as the Spanish colony of Santo Domingo.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-google48_53-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-google48-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="French_rule_.281795.E2.80.931809.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="French_rule_(1795–1809)">
        French rule (1795–1809)
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       France came to own Hispaniola in 1795 when by the
       <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Basel" title="Peace of Basel">
        Peace of Basel
       </a>
       Spain ceded Santo Domingo as a consequence of the
       <a href="/wiki/French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="French Revolutionary Wars">
        French Revolutionary Wars
       </a>
       . The recently freed Africans led by
       <a href="/wiki/Toussaint_Louverture" title="Toussaint Louverture">
        Toussaint Louverture
       </a>
       in 1801, took over Santo Domingo in the east, thus gaining control of the entire island. In 1802 an army sent by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napoleon_I" title="Napoleon I">
        Napoleon
       </a>
       captured Toussaint Louverture and sent him to France as prisoner. Toussaint Louverture’s lieutenants and the spread of
       <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">
        yellow fever
       </a>
       succeeded in driving the French again from Saint-Domingue, which in 1804 the rebels made independent as the Republic of Haiti. Eastwards, France continued to rule Spanish Santo Domingo.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1805, Haitian troops of general
       <a href="/wiki/Henri_Christophe" title="Henri Christophe">
        Henri Christophe
       </a>
       invaded Santo Domingo and sacked the towns of Santiago de los Caballeros and
       <a href="/wiki/Moca,_Dominican_Republic" title="Moca, Dominican Republic">
        Moca
       </a>
       , killing most of their residents and helping to lay the foundation for two centuries of animosity between the two countries.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1808, following
       <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">
        Napoleon's invasion of Spain
       </a>
       , the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Criollo_(people)" title="Criollo (people)">
         criollos
        </a>
       </i>
       of Santo Domingo revolted against French rule and, with the aid of the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">
        United Kingdom
       </a>
       (Spain's ally) returned Santo Domingo to
       <a href="/wiki/Espa%C3%B1a_Boba" title="España Boba">
        Spanish control
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica_54-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Britannica-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Independence_from_Spain_.281821.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_from_Spain_(1821)">
        Independence from Spain (1821)
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Spanish_Haiti" title="Republic of Spanish Haiti">
        Republic of Spanish Haiti
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       After a dozen years of discontent and failed independence plots by various opposing groups, Santo Domingo's former Lieutenant-Governor (top administrator),
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_N%C3%BA%C3%B1ez_de_C%C3%A1ceres" title="José Núñez de Cáceres">
        José Núñez de Cáceres
       </a>
       , declared the colony's independence from the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">
        Spanish crown
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Spanish_Haiti" title="Republic of Spanish Haiti">
        Spanish Haiti
       </a>
       , on November 30, 1821. This period is also known as the Ephemeral independence.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bethell1986_55-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bethell1986-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Unification_of_Hispaniola_.281822.E2.80.9344.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Unification_of_Hispaniola_(1822–44)">
        Unification of Hispaniola (1822–44)
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Unification_of_Hispaniola" title="Unification of Hispaniola">
        Unification of Hispaniola
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_(Hispaniola_Unification_Regime)_Portrait.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="560" data-file-width="460" height="219" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_%28Hispaniola_Unification_Regime%29_Portrait.jpg/180px-President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_%28Hispaniola_Unification_Regime%29_Portrait.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_%28Hispaniola_Unification_Regime%29_Portrait.jpg/270px-President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_%28Hispaniola_Unification_Regime%29_Portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_%28Hispaniola_Unification_Regime%29_Portrait.jpg/360px-President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_%28Hispaniola_Unification_Regime%29_Portrait.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_(Hispaniola_Unification_Regime)_Portrait.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Boyer" title="Jean-Pierre Boyer">
          Jean-Pierre Boyer
         </a>
         , the ruler of Haiti
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The newly independent republic ended two months later under the Haitian government led by
       <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Boyer" title="Jean-Pierre Boyer">
        Jean-Pierre Boyer
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guitar_56-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-guitar-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As Toussaint Louverture had done two decades earlier, the Haitians abolished slavery. In order to raise funds for the huge indemnity of 150 million francs that Haiti agreed to pay the former French colonists, and which was subsequently lowered to 60 million francs, the Haitian government imposed heavy taxes on the Dominicans. Since Haiti was unable to adequately provision its army, the occupying forces largely survived by commandeering or confiscating food and supplies at gunpoint. Attempts to
       <a href="/wiki/Land_reform" title="Land reform">
        redistribute
       </a>
       land conflicted with the system of communal land tenure (
       <i>
        terrenos comuneros
       </i>
       ), which had arisen with the ranching economy, and some people resented being forced to grow cash crops under Boyer and
       <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Balthazar_Inginac" title="Joseph Balthazar Inginac">
        Joseph Balthazar Inginac
       </a>
       's
       <i>
        Code Rural
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the rural and rugged mountainous areas, the Haitian administration was usually too inefficient to enforce its own laws. It was in the city of Santo Domingo that the effects of the occupation were most acutely felt, and it was there that the movement for independence originated.
      </p>
      <p>
       Haiti's constitution forbade white elites from owning land, and Dominican major landowning families were forcibly deprived of their properties. Many emigrated to
       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
        Cuba
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">
        Puerto Rico
       </a>
       (these two being
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">
        Spanish possessions
       </a>
       at the time), or
       <a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">
        Gran Colombia
       </a>
       , usually with the encouragement of Haitian officials who acquired their lands. The Haitians associated the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">
        Roman Catholic Church
       </a>
       with the French slave-masters who had exploited them before independence and confiscated all church property, deported all foreign clergy, and severed the ties of the remaining clergy to the
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">
        Vatican
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       All levels of education collapsed; the university was shut down, as it was starved both of resources and students, with young Dominican men from 16 to 25 years old being drafted into the Haitian army. Boyer's occupation troops, who were largely Dominicans, were unpaid and had to "forage and sack" from Dominican civilians. Haiti imposed a "heavy tribute" on the Dominican people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Matibag_58-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Matibag-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         page number needed
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Many whites fled Santo Domingo for
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">
        Puerto Rico
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
        Cuba
       </a>
       (both still under Spanish rule),
       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
        Venezuela
       </a>
       , and elsewhere. In the end the economy faltered and taxation became more onerous. Rebellions occurred even by Dominican freedmen, while Dominicans and Haitians worked together to oust Boyer from power. Anti-Haitian movements of several kinds – pro-independence, pro-Spanish, pro-French, pro-British, pro-United States – gathered force following the overthrow of Boyer in 1843.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Matibag_58-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Matibag-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         page number needed
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Independence_from_Haiti_.281844.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_from_Haiti_(1844)">
        Independence from Haiti (1844)
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Dominican_War_of_Independence" title="Dominican War of Independence">
        Dominican War of Independence
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Juan_pablo_duarte_diez.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="806" data-file-width="600" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Juan_pablo_duarte_diez.jpg/170px-Juan_pablo_duarte_diez.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Juan_pablo_duarte_diez.jpg/255px-Juan_pablo_duarte_diez.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Juan_pablo_duarte_diez.jpg/340px-Juan_pablo_duarte_diez.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Juan_pablo_duarte_diez.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Juan_Pablo_Duarte" title="Juan Pablo Duarte">
          Juan Pablo Duarte
         </a>
         , founding father of the Dominican Republic
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Francisco_del_Rosario.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="460" data-file-width="301" height="260" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Francisco_del_Rosario.jpg/170px-Francisco_del_Rosario.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Francisco_del_Rosario.jpg/255px-Francisco_del_Rosario.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f6/Francisco_del_Rosario.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Francisco_del_Rosario.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Francisco_del_Rosario_S%C3%A1nchez" title="Francisco del Rosario Sánchez">
          Francisco del Rosario Sánchez
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1838
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Pablo_Duarte" title="Juan Pablo Duarte">
        Juan Pablo Duarte
       </a>
       founded a secret society called
       <a href="/wiki/La_Trinitaria_(Dominican_Republic)" title="La Trinitaria (Dominican Republic)">
        La Trinitaria
       </a>
       , which sought the complete independence of Santo Domingo without any foreign intervention.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pons_59-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-pons-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         p147–149
        </span>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Mat%C3%ADas_Ram%C3%B3n_Mella" title="Matías Ramón Mella">
        Matías Ramón Mella
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_del_Rosario_S%C3%A1nchez" title="Francisco del Rosario Sánchez">
        Francisco del Rosario Sánchez
       </a>
       , despite not being among the founding members of La Trinitaria, were decisive in the fight for independence. Duarte, Mella, and Sánchez are considered the three Founding Fathers of the Dominican Republic.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On February 27, 1844, the
       <i>
        Trinitarios
       </i>
       (the members of La Trinitaria), declared the independence from Haiti. They were backed by
       <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Santana" title="Pedro Santana">
        Pedro Santana
       </a>
       , a wealthy cattle rancher from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Seibo" title="El Seibo">
        El Seibo
       </a>
       , who became general of the army of the nascent republic. The Dominican Republic's first
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Dominican_Republic" title="Constitution of the Dominican Republic">
        Constitution
       </a>
       was adopted on November 6, 1844, and was modeled after the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">
        United States Constitution
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_34-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Encarta-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The decades that followed were filled with tyranny, factionalism, economic difficulties, rapid changes of government, and exile for political opponents. Threatening the nation's independence were renewed Haitian invasions occurring in 1844, 1845–49, 1849–55, and 1855–56.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Matibag_58-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Matibag-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         page number needed
        </span>
       </sup>
       Haiti did not recognize the Dominican Republic until 1874.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mirex2000_4-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-mirex2000-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Autores2012_61-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Autores2012-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Meanwhile, archrivals Santana and
       <a href="/wiki/Buenaventura_B%C3%A1ez" title="Buenaventura Báez">
        Buenaventura Báez
       </a>
       held power most of the time, both ruling arbitrarily. They promoted competing plans to annex the new nation to another power: Santana favored Spain, and Báez the United States.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Restoration_republic">
        Restoration republic
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Restoration_War" title="Dominican Restoration War">
        Dominican Restoration War
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GregorioLuperon.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="448" data-file-width="356" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/GregorioLuperon.jpg/150px-GregorioLuperon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/GregorioLuperon.jpg/225px-GregorioLuperon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/GregorioLuperon.jpg/300px-GregorioLuperon.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GregorioLuperon.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Gregorio_Luper%C3%B3n" title="Gregorio Luperón">
          General Gregorio Luperón
         </a>
         , Restoration hero and later President of the Republic
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1861, after imprisoning, silencing, exiling, and executing many of his opponents and due to political and economic reasons, Santana signed a pact with the Spanish Crown and reverted the Dominican nation to colonial status, the only Latin American country to do so. His ostensible aim was to protect the nation from another Haitian annexation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sagas_62-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Sagas-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Opponents launched the
       <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Restoration_War" title="Dominican Restoration War">
        War of Restoration
       </a>
       in 1863, led by
       <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Masag%C3%B3" title="Santiago Rodríguez Masagó">
        Santiago Rodríguez
       </a>
       , Benito Monción, and
       <a href="/wiki/Gregorio_Luper%C3%B3n" title="Gregorio Luperón">
        Gregorio Luperón
       </a>
       , among others. Haiti, fearful of the re-establishment of Spain as colonial power on its border, gave refuge and supplies to the revolutionaries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sagas_62-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Sagas-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The United States, then fighting its own
       <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">
        Civil War
       </a>
       , vigorously protested the Spanish action. After two years of fighting, Spain abandoned the island in 1865.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sagas_62-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Sagas-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Political strife again prevailed in the following years; warlords ruled, military revolts were extremely common, and the nation amassed debt. It was now Báez's turn to act on his
       <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Santo_Domingo" title="Annexation of Santo Domingo">
        plan of annexing the country to the United States
       </a>
       , where two successive presidents were supportive.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_34-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Encarta-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guitar_56-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-guitar-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       U.S. President Grant desired a naval base at
       <a href="/wiki/Saman%C3%A1_Bay" title="Samaná Bay">
        Samaná
       </a>
       and also a place for resettling newly freed
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">
        Blacks
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The treaty, which included U.S. payment of $1.5 million for Dominican debt repayment, was defeated in the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">
        United States Senate
       </a>
       in 1870
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guitar_56-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-guitar-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       on a vote of 28–28, two-thirds being required.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hereaux2.gif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="429" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Hereaux2.gif/150px-Hereaux2.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Hereaux2.gif/225px-Hereaux2.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Hereaux2.gif/300px-Hereaux2.gif 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hereaux2.gif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Ulises_Heureaux" title="Ulises Heureaux">
          Ulises 'Lilís' Heureaux
         </a>
         , President of the Republic 1882–84, 1886–99
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Báez was toppled in 1874, returned, and was toppled for good in 1878. A new generation was thence in charge, with the passing of Santana (he died in 1864) and Báez from the scene. Relative peace came to the country in the 1880s, which saw the coming to power of General
       <a href="/wiki/Ulises_Heureaux" title="Ulises Heureaux">
        Ulises Heureaux
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-countrystudies_68-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       "Lilís," as the new president was nicknamed, enjoyed a period of popularity. He was, however, "a consummate dissembler," who put the nation deep into debt while using much of the proceeds for his personal use and to maintain his police state. Heureaux became rampantly despotic and unpopular.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-countrystudies_68-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1899 he was assassinated. However, the relative calm over which he presided allowed improvement in the Dominican economy. The sugar industry was modernized,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hall_70-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hall-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         p10
        </span>
       </sup>
       and the country attracted foreign workers and immigrants.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="20th_century_.281900.E2.80.9330.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century_(1900–30)">
        20th century (1900–30)
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alejandro_Woss_y_Gil.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="550" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Alejandro_Woss_y_Gil.jpg/220px-Alejandro_Woss_y_Gil.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Alejandro_Woss_y_Gil.jpg/330px-Alejandro_Woss_y_Gil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Alejandro_Woss_y_Gil.jpg/440px-Alejandro_Woss_y_Gil.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alejandro_Woss_y_Gil.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         President
         <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Woss_y_Gil" title="Alejandro Woss y Gil">
          Alejandro Woss y Gil
         </a>
         taking office in 1903
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       From 1902 on, short-lived governments were again the norm, with their power usurped by
       <a href="/wiki/Caudillo" title="Caudillo">
        caudillos
       </a>
       in parts of the country. Furthermore, the national government was bankrupt and, unable to pay Heureaux's debts, faced the threat of military intervention by France and other European creditor powers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cs9_71-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cs9-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       United States President
       <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">
        Theodore Roosevelt
       </a>
       sought to prevent European intervention, largely to protect the routes to the future
       <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal" title="Panama Canal">
        Panama Canal
       </a>
       , as the canal was already under construction. He made a small
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1916_United_States_occupation_of_the_Dominican_Republic" title="1916 United States occupation of the Dominican Republic">
        military intervention
       </a>
       to ward off European powers, to proclaim his famous
       <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Corollary" title="Roosevelt Corollary">
        Roosevelt Corollary
       </a>
       to the
       <a href="/wiki/Monroe_Doctrine" title="Monroe Doctrine">
        Monroe Doctrine
       </a>
       , and also to obtain his 1905 Dominican agreement for U.S. administration of Dominican customs, which was the chief source of income for the Dominican government. A 1906 agreement provided for the arrangement to last 50 years. The United States agreed to use part of the customs proceeds to reduce the immense foreign debt of the Dominican Republic and assumed responsibility for said debt.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_34-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Encarta-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cs9_71-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-cs9-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ramon_Caceres.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="585" data-file-width="574" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Ramon_Caceres.jpg/150px-Ramon_Caceres.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Ramon_Caceres.jpg/225px-Ramon_Caceres.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Ramon_Caceres.jpg/300px-Ramon_Caceres.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ramon_Caceres.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_C%C3%A1ceres" title="Ramón Cáceres">
          Ramón Cáceres
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       After six years in power, President
       <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_C%C3%A1ceres" title="Ramón Cáceres">
        Ramón Cáceres
       </a>
       (who had himself assassinated Heureaux)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-countrystudies_68-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       was assassinated in 1911. The result was several years of great political instability and civil war. U.S. mediation by the
       <a href="/wiki/William_Howard_Taft" title="William Howard Taft">
        William Howard Taft
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">
        Woodrow Wilson
       </a>
       administrations achieved only a short respite each time. A political deadlock in 1914 was broken after an ultimatum by Wilson telling the Dominicans to choose a president or see the U.S. impose one. A provisional president was chosen, and later the same year relatively free elections put former president (1899–1902)
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Isidro_Jimenes_Pereyra" title="Juan Isidro Jimenes Pereyra">
        Juan Isidro Jimenes Pereyra
       </a>
       back in power. To achieve a more broadly supported government, Jimenes named opposition individuals to his cabinet. But this brought no peace and, with his former
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secretary_of_War" title="Secretary of War">
        Secretary of War
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Desiderio_Arias" title="Desiderio Arias">
        Desiderio Arias
       </a>
       maneuvering to depose him and despite a U.S. offer of military aid against Arias, Jimenes resigned on May 7, 1916.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-congress_72-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-congress-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Wilson thus ordered the U.S. occupation of the Dominican Republic.
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">
        U.S. Marines
       </a>
       landed on May 16, 1916, and had control of the country two months later. The military government established by the U.S., led by Vice Admiral
       <a href="/wiki/Harry_Shepard_Knapp" title="Harry Shepard Knapp">
        Harry Shepard Knapp
       </a>
       , was widely repudiated by the Dominicans, with many factions within the country leading guerrilla campaigns against U.S. forces.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-congress_72-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-congress-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The occupation regime kept most Dominican laws and institutions and largely pacified the general population. The occupying government also revived the Dominican economy, reduced the nation's debt, built a road network that at last interconnected all regions of the country, and created a professional National Guard to replace the warring partisan units.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-congress_72-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-congress-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Vigorous opposition to the occupation continued, nevertheless, and after World War I it increased in the U.S. as well. There, President
       <a href="/wiki/Warren_G._Harding" title="Warren G. Harding">
        Warren G. Harding
       </a>
       (1921–23), Wilson's successor, worked to put an end to the occupation, as he had promised to do during his campaign. The U.S. government's rule ended in October 1922, and elections were held in March 1924.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-congress_72-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-congress-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Horacio_Vasquez.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="304" data-file-width="340" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Horacio_Vasquez.jpg/200px-Horacio_Vasquez.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Horacio_Vasquez.jpg/300px-Horacio_Vasquez.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/dc/Horacio_Vasquez.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Horacio_Vasquez.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Horacio_V%C3%A1squez" title="Horacio Vásquez">
          Horacio Vásquez Lajara
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The victor was former president (1902–03)
       <a href="/wiki/Horacio_V%C3%A1squez" title="Horacio Vásquez">
        Horacio Vásquez Lajara
       </a>
       , who had cooperated with the U.S. He was inaugurated on July 13, and the last U.S. forces left in September. Vásquez gave the country six years of stable governance, in which political and civil rights were respected and the economy grew strongly, in a relatively peaceful atmosphere.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-congress_72-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-congress-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-locdr11_73-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-locdr11-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During the government of Horacio Vásquez,
       <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Trujillo" title="Rafael Trujillo">
        Rafael Trujillo
       </a>
       held the rank of lieutenant colonel and was chief of police. This position helped him launch his plans to overthrow the government of Vásquez. Trujillo had the support of Carlos Rosario Peña, who formed the Civic Movement, which had as its main objective to overthrow the government of Vásquez.
      </p>
      <p>
       In February 1930, when Vásquez attempted to win another term, his opponents rebelled in secret alliance with the commander of the National Army (the former National Guard), General
       <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Trujillo" title="Rafael Trujillo">
        Rafael Leonidas Trujillo Molina
       </a>
       . Trujillo secretly cut a deal with rebel leader
       <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Estrella_Ure%C3%B1a" title="Rafael Estrella Ureña">
        Rafael Estrella Ureña
       </a>
       ; in return for letting Ureña take power, Trujillo would be allowed to run for president in new elections. As the rebels marched toward Santo Domingo, Vásquez ordered Trujillo to suppress them. However, feigning "neutrality," Trujillo kept his men in barracks, allowing Ureña's rebels to take the capital virtually uncontested. On March 3, Ureña was proclaimed acting president with Trujillo confirmed as head of the police and the army.
      </p>
      <p>
       As per their agreement, Trujillo became the presidential nominee of the newly formed Patriotic Coalition of Citizens (Spanish: Coalición patriotica de los ciudadanos), with Ureña as his running mate. During the election campaign, Trujillo used the army to unleash his repression, forcing his opponents to withdraw from the race. Trujillo stood to elect himself, and in May he was elected president virtually unopposed after a violent campaign against his opponents, ascending to power on August 16, 1930.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Trujillo_Age_.281930.E2.80.9361.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Trujillo_Age_(1930–61)">
        Trujillo Age (1930–61)
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       There was considerable economic growth during
       <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Trujillo" title="Rafael Trujillo">
        Rafael Trujillo
       </a>
       's long and iron-fisted regime, although a great deal of the wealth was taken by the dictator and other regime elements. There was progress in healthcare, education, and transportation, with the building of hospitals and clinics, schools, and roads and harbors. Trujillo also carried out an important housing construction program and instituted a pension plan. He finally negotiated an undisputed border with Haiti in 1935 and achieved the end of the 50-year customs agreement in 1941, instead of 1956. He made the country debt-free in 1947.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_34-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-Encarta-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       This was accompanied by absolute repression and the copious use of murder, torture, and terrorist methods against the opposition. Trujillo renamed
       <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">
        Santo Domingo
       </a>
       to "Ciudad Trujillo" (Trujillo City),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_34-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-Encarta-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the nation's – and the Caribbean's – highest mountain
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Pico_Duarte" title="Pico Duarte">
         La Pelona Grande
        </a>
       </i>
       (Spanish for: The Great Bald) to "Pico Trujillo" (Spanish for: Trujillo Peak), and many towns and a province. Some other places he renamed after members of his family. By the end of his first term in 1934 he was the country's wealthiest person,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pons_59-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-pons-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         p360
        </span>
       </sup>
       and one of the wealthiest in the world by the early 1950s;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       near the end of his regime his fortune was an estimated $800 million.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hall_70-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hall-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         p111
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Although one-quarter Haitian, Trujillo promoted propaganda against them.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-killer_75-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-killer-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1937, he ordered what became known as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parsley_Massacre" title="Parsley Massacre">
        Parsley Massacre
       </a>
       or, in the Dominican Republic, as
       <i>
        El Corte
       </i>
       (The Cutting),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wucker_76-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Wucker-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       directing the army to kill Haitians living on the Dominican side of the border. The army killed an estimated 17,000 to 35,000 Haitians over six days, from the night of October 2, 1937, through October 8, 1937. To avoid leaving evidence of the army's involvement, the soldiers used
       <a href="/wiki/Machete" title="Machete">
        machetes
       </a>
       rather than bullets.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guitar_56-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-guitar-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-killer_75-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-killer-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The soldiers were said to have interrogated anyone with dark skin, using the
       <a href="/wiki/Shibboleth" title="Shibboleth">
        shibboleth
       </a>
       <i>
        perejil
       </i>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Parsley" title="Parsley">
        parsley
       </a>
       ) to distinguish Haitians from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-Dominican_(Dominican_Republic)" title="Afro-Dominican (Dominican Republic)">
        Afro-Dominicans
       </a>
       when necessary; the 'r' of
       <i>
        perejil
       </i>
       was of difficult pronunciation for Haitians.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wucker_76-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Wucker-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As a result of the massacre, the Dominican Republic agreed to pay Haiti US$750,000, later reduced to US$525,000.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sagas_62-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Sagas-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-locdr11_73-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-locdr11-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On November 25, 1960, Trujillo killed three of the four
       <a href="/wiki/Mirabal_sisters" title="Mirabal sisters">
        Mirabal sisters
       </a>
       , nicknamed
       <i>
        Las Mariposas
       </i>
       (The Butterflies). The victims were Patria Mercedes Mirabal (born on February 27, 1924), Argentina Minerva Mirabal (born on March 12, 1926), and Antonia María Teresa Mirabal (born on October 15, 1935). Along with their husbands, the sisters were conspiring to overthrow Trujillo in a violent revolt. The Mirabals had communist ideological leanings as did their husbands. The sisters have received many honors posthumously and have many memorials in various cities in the Dominican Republic. Salcedo, their home province, changed its name to
       <a href="/wiki/Hermanas_Mirabal_Province" title="Hermanas Mirabal Province">
        Provincia Hermanas Mirabal
       </a>
       (Mirabal Sisters Province). The
       <a href="/wiki/International_Day_for_the_Elimination_of_Violence_against_Women" title="International Day for the Elimination of Violence against Women">
        International Day for the Elimination of Violence against Women
       </a>
       is observed on the anniversary of their deaths.
      </p>
      <p>
       For a long time, the U.S. and the Dominican elite supported the Trujillo government. This support persisted despite the assassinations of political opposition, the massacre of Haitians, and Trujillo's plots against other countries. The U.S. believed Trujillo was the lesser of two or more evils.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wucker_76-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Wucker-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The U.S. finally broke with Trujillo in 1960, after Trujillo's agents attempted to assassinate the Venezuelan president,
       <a href="/wiki/R%C3%B3mulo_Betancourt" title="Rómulo Betancourt">
        Rómulo Betancourt
       </a>
       , a fierce critic of Trujillo.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-locdr11_73-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-locdr11-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Post-Trujillo_.281961.E2.80.932000.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Trujillo_(1961–2000)">
        Post-Trujillo (1961–2000)
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Juan_Bosch_(1963).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1055" data-file-width="791" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Juan_Bosch_%281963%29.jpg/150px-Juan_Bosch_%281963%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Juan_Bosch_%281963%29.jpg/225px-Juan_Bosch_%281963%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Juan_Bosch_%281963%29.jpg/300px-Juan_Bosch_%281963%29.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Juan_Bosch_(1963).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Juan Bosch, the first democratically elected president after the regime of Rafael Trujillo
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Trujillo was assassinated on May 30, 1961.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-locdr11_73-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-locdr11-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In February 1963, a democratically elected government under leftist
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Bosch" title="Juan Bosch">
        Juan Bosch
       </a>
       took office but it was overthrown in September. In April 1965, after 19 months of military rule, a pro-Bosch revolt broke out.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Days later U.S. President
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lyndon_Johnson" title="Lyndon Johnson">
        Lyndon Johnson
       </a>
       , concerned that Communists might take over the revolt and create a "second Cuba," sent the Marines, followed immediately by the U.S. Army's
       <a href="/wiki/82nd_Airborne_Division" title="82nd Airborne Division">
        82nd Airborne Division
       </a>
       and other elements of the XVIIIth Airborne Corps, in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Powerpack" title="Operation Powerpack">
        Operation Powerpack
       </a>
       . "We don't propose to sit here in a rocking chair with our hands folded and let the Communist set up any government in the western hemisphere," Johnson said.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The forces were soon joined by comparatively small contingents from the
       <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">
        Organization of American States
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-civil_war_81-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-civil_war-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       All these remained in the country for over a year and left after supervising elections in 1966 won by
       <a href="/wiki/Joaqu%C3%ADn_Balaguer" title="Joaquín Balaguer">
        Joaquín Balaguer
       </a>
       . He had been Trujillo's last puppet-president.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_34-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-Encarta-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-civil_war_81-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-civil_war-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
