         </div>
         Dominican Republic people in the town of
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moca,_Espaillat" title="Moca, Espaillat">
          Moca
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Dominican Republic's population is 73% of racially mixed origin, 16%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Dominican_(Dominican_Republic)" title="White Dominican (Dominican Republic)">
        White
       </a>
       , and 11% Black.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIADemo_6-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIADemo-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Ethnic immigrant groups in the country include
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southwest_Asia" title="Southwest Asia">
        West Asians
       </a>
       —mostly
       <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_people" title="Lebanese people">
        Lebanese
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syrian_people" title="Syrian people">
        Syrians
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" title="Palestinian people">
        Palestinians
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Levinson_124-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Levinson-124">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Numerous immigrants have come from other Caribbean countries, as the country has offered economic opportunities. There are about 32,000
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaicans" title="Jamaicans">
        Jamaicans
       </a>
       living in the Dominican Republic.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
        <a href="#cite_note-125">
         [125]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There is an increasing number of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_people" title="Puerto Rican people">
        Puerto Rican
       </a>
       immigrants, especially in and around
       <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">
        Santo Domingo
       </a>
       ; they are believed to number around 10,000.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
        <a href="#cite_note-126">
         [126]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
        <a href="#cite_note-127">
         [127]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are over 700,000 people of Haitian descent, including a generation born in the Dominican Republic.
      </p>
      <p>
       East Asians, primarily
       <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_Chinese_in_the_Dominican_Republic" title="Ethnic Chinese in the Dominican Republic">
        ethnic Chinese
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Japanese_settlement_in_the_Dominican_Republic" title="Japanese settlement in the Dominican Republic">
        Japanese,
       </a>
       can also be found.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Levinson_124-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Levinson-124">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Europeans are represented mostly by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_people" title="Spanish people">
        Spanish
       </a>
       whites but also with smaller populations of
       <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews" title="Ashkenazi Jews">
        German Jews
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_people" title="Italian people">
        Italians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/British_people" title="British people">
        British
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">
        Dutch
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Danes" title="Danes">
        Danes
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hungarian_people" title="Hungarian people">
        Hungarians
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Levinson_124-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Levinson-124">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
        <a href="#cite_note-128">
         [128]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SosuaJewishStudies_129-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-SosuaJewishStudies-129">
         [129]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some converted
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sephardic_Jews" title="Sephardic Jews">
        Sephardic Jews
       </a>
       from Spain were part of early expeditions; only Catholics were allowed to come to the New World.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
        <a href="#cite_note-130">
         [130]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Later there were Jewish migrants coming from Iberia and Europe in the 1700s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
        <a href="#cite_note-131">
         [131]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some managed to reach the Caribbean as refugees during and after the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">
        Second World War
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
        <a href="#cite_note-132">
         [132]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
        <a href="#cite_note-133">
         [133]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
        <a href="#cite_note-134">
         [134]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some Sephardic Jews reside in
       <a href="/wiki/Sos%C3%BAa" title="Sosúa">
        Sosúa
       </a>
       while others are dispersed throughout the country.
       <a href="/wiki/Who_is_a_Jew%3F" title="Who is a Jew?">
        Self-identified Jews
       </a>
       number about 3,000; other Dominicans may have some Jewish ancestry because of marriages among converted Jewish Catholics and other Dominicans since the colonial years. Some Dominicans born in the United States now reside in the Dominican Republic, creating a kind of expatriate community.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
        <a href="#cite_note-135">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">
        Languages
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Spanish" title="Dominican Spanish">
        Dominican Spanish
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Saman%C3%A1_English" title="Samaná English">
        Samaná English
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The population of the Dominican Republic is mostly
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       -speaking. The local
       <a href="/wiki/Variation_(linguistics)" title="Variation (linguistics)">
        variant
       </a>
       of Spanish is called
       <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Spanish" title="Dominican Spanish">
        Dominican Spanish
       </a>
       , which closely resembles other Spanish
       <a href="/wiki/Vernacular" title="Vernacular">
        vernaculars
       </a>
       in the Caribbean and the
       <a href="/wiki/Canarian_Spanish" title="Canarian Spanish">
        Canarian Spanish
       </a>
       . In addition, it borrowed words from
       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas#South_America_and_the_Caribbean" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">
        indigenous Caribbean languages
       </a>
       particular to the island of Hispaniola.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
        <a href="#cite_note-136">
         [136]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
        <a href="#cite_note-137">
         [137]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Schools are based on a Spanish educational model; English and French are mandatory foreign languages in both private and public schools,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
        <a href="#cite_note-138">
         [138]
        </a>
       </sup>
       although the quality of foreign languages teaching is poor.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
        <a href="#cite_note-139">
         [139]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some private educational institutes provide teaching on other languages, notably Italian, Japanese, and Mandarin.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
        <a href="#cite_note-140">
         [140]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
        <a href="#cite_note-141">
         [141]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Creole" title="Haitian Creole">
        Haitian Creole
       </a>
       is the largest minority language in the Dominican Republic and is spoken by
       <a href="/wiki/Haitians" title="Haitians">
        Haitian
       </a>
       immigrants and their descendants.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
        <a href="#cite_note-142">
         [142]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There is a community of a few thousand people whose ancestors spoke
       <a href="/wiki/Saman%C3%A1_English" title="Samaná English">
        Samaná English
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Saman%C3%A1_Peninsula" title="Samaná Peninsula">
        Samaná Peninsula
       </a>
       . They are the descendants of formerly enslaved African Americans who arrived in the nineteenth century, but only a few elders speak the language today.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
        <a href="#cite_note-143">
         [143]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Tourism, American pop culture, the influence of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominican_American" title="Dominican American">
        Dominican Americans
       </a>
       , and the country's economic ties with the United States motivate other Dominicans to learn English. The Dominican Republic is ranked 2
       <sup>
        <small>
         nd
        </small>
       </sup>
       in Latin America and 23
       <sup>
        <small>
         rd
        </small>
       </sup>
       in the World on English
       <a href="/wiki/Language_proficiency" title="Language proficiency">
        proficiency
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">
        <a href="#cite_note-144">
         [144]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">
        <a href="#cite_note-145">
         [145]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable sortable">

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
        Religion
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_the_Dominican_Republic" title="Religion in the Dominican Republic">
        Religion in the Dominican Republic
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bas%C3%ADlica_Menor_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_SD_RD_02_2017_1941.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2765" data-file-width="4201" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Bas%C3%ADlica_Menor_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_SD_RD_02_2017_1941.jpg/300px-Bas%C3%ADlica_Menor_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_SD_RD_02_2017_1941.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Bas%C3%ADlica_Menor_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_SD_RD_02_2017_1941.jpg/450px-Bas%C3%ADlica_Menor_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_SD_RD_02_2017_1941.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Bas%C3%ADlica_Menor_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_SD_RD_02_2017_1941.jpg/600px-Bas%C3%ADlica_Menor_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_SD_RD_02_2017_1941.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bas%C3%ADlica_Menor_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_SD_RD_02_2017_1941.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_la_Menor" title="Cathedral of Santa María la Menor">
          Cathedral of Santa María la Menor
         </a>
         , Santo Domingo, the oldest cathedral in the Americas, built 1512–1540
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <b>
        95.0%
       </b>
       Christians
       <br/>
       <b>
        2.6%
       </b>
       No religion
       <br/>
       <b>
        2.2%
       </b>
       Other religions
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">
        <a href="#cite_note-148">
         [148]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As of 2014, 57% of the population (5.7 million) identified themselves as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholics" title="Roman Catholics">
        Roman Catholics
       </a>
       and 23% (2.3 million) as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestants" title="Protestants">
        Protestants
       </a>
       (in Latin American countries, Protestants are often called
       <i>
        Evangelicos
       </i>
       because they emphasize personal and public evangelising and many are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evangelical_Protestant" title="Evangelical Protestant">
        Evangelical Protestant
       </a>
       or of a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pentecostal" title="Pentecostal">
        Pentecostal
       </a>
       group). From 1896 to 1907 missionaries from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Episcopal_Church" title="The Episcopal Church">
        Episcopal
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_Methodist" title="Free Methodist">
        Free Methodist
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist" title="Seventh-day Adventist">
        Seventh-day Adventist
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Moravians" title="Moravians">
        Moravians
       </a>
       churches began work in the Dominican Republic.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Religious_Transformations_149-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Religious_Transformations-149">
         [149]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">
        <a href="#cite_note-150">
         [150]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">
        <a href="#cite_note-151">
         [151]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Three percent of the 10.63 million Dominican Republic population are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventists" title="Seventh-day Adventists">
        Seventh-day Adventists
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">
        <a href="#cite_note-152">
         [152]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Recent immigration as well as proselytizing efforts have brought in other religious groups, with the following shares of the population:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spiritist" title="Spiritist">
        Spiritist
       </a>
       : 2.2%,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-religiousfreedom_153-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-religiousfreedom-153">
         [153]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">
        The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints
       </a>
       : 1.1%,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ldsnewsroom_154-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ldsnewsroom-154">
         [154]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">
        Buddhist
       </a>
       : 0.1%,
       <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bahá'í Faith">
        Bahá'í
       </a>
       : 0.1%,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-religiousfreedom_153-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-religiousfreedom-153">
         [153]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Folk_Religion" title="Chinese Folk Religion">
        Chinese Folk Religion
       </a>
       : 0.1%,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-religiousfreedom_153-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-religiousfreedom-153">
         [153]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Islam: 0.02%, Judaism: 0.01%.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Catholic Church began to lose its strong dominance in the late 19th century. This was due to a lack of funding, priests, and support programs. During the same time,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">
        Protestant
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">
        Evangelicalism
       </a>
       began to gain a wider support "with their emphasis on personal responsibility and family rejuvenation, economic entrepreneurship, and biblical
       <a href="/wiki/Fundamentalism" title="Fundamentalism">
        fundamentalism
       </a>
       ".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">
        <a href="#cite_note-155">
         [155]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Dominican Republic has two Catholic patroness saints:
       <i>
        Nuestra Señora de la Altagracia
       </i>
       (Our Lady Of High Grace) and
       <i>
        Nuestra Señora de las Mercedes
       </i>
       (Our Lady Of Mercy).
      </p>
      <p>
       The Dominican Republic has historically granted extensive religious freedom. According to the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">
        United States Department of State
       </a>
       , "The constitution specifies that there is no state church and provides for freedom of religion and belief. A concordat with the Vatican designates Catholicism as the official religion and extends special privileges to the Catholic Church not granted to other religious groups. These include the legal recognition of church law, use of public funds to underwrite some church expenses, and complete exoneration from customs duties."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">
        <a href="#cite_note-156">
         [156]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the 1950s restrictions were placed upon churches by the government of Trujillo. Letters of protest were sent against the mass arrests of government adversaries. Trujillo began a campaign against the Catholic Church and planned to arrest priests and bishops who preached against the government. This campaign ended before it was put into place, with his assassination.
      </p>
      <p>
       During World War II a group of Jews escaping
       <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">
        Nazi Germany
       </a>
       fled to the Dominican Republic and founded the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Sos%C3%BAa" title="Sosúa">
        Sosúa
       </a>
       . It has remained the center of the Jewish population since.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">
        <a href="#cite_note-157">
         [157]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century_immigration">
        20th century immigration
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Japanese_settlement_in_the_Dominican_Republic" title="Japanese settlement in the Dominican Republic">
        Japanese settlement in the Dominican Republic
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_Chinese_in_the_Dominican_Republic" title="Ethnic Chinese in the Dominican Republic">
        Ethnic Chinese in the Dominican Republic
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_the_Dominican_Republic" title="History of the Jews in the Dominican Republic">
        History of the Jews in the Dominican Republic
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Colonia_Japonesa.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="516" data-file-width="800" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Colonia_Japonesa.jpg/300px-Colonia_Japonesa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Colonia_Japonesa.jpg/450px-Colonia_Japonesa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Colonia_Japonesa.jpg/600px-Colonia_Japonesa.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Colonia_Japonesa.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Family of
         <a href="/wiki/Japanese_diaspora" title="Japanese diaspora">
          Japanese descent
         </a>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/Constanza,_Dominican_Republic" title="Constanza, Dominican Republic">
          Constanza
         </a>
         's neighbourhood of
         <a href="/wiki/Japanese_settlement_in_the_Dominican_Republic" title="Japanese settlement in the Dominican Republic">
          Colonia Japonesa
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the 20th century, many
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab" title="Arab">
        Arabs
       </a>
       (from
       <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">
        Lebanon
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
        Syria
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Palestine_(region)" title="Palestine (region)">
        Palestine
       </a>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lebanon-migrants-register_158-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Lebanon-migrants-register-158">
         [158]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Japanese, and, to a lesser degree,
       <a href="/wiki/Koreans" title="Koreans">
        Koreans
       </a>
       settled in the country as agricultural laborers and merchants. The Chinese companies found business in telecom, mining, and railroads. The Arab community is rising at an increasing rate and is estimated at 80,000.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lebanon-migrants-register_158-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Lebanon-migrants-register-158">
         [158]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In addition, there are descendants of immigrants who came from other Caribbean islands, including
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Kitts_and_Nevis" title="St. Kitts and Nevis">
        St. Kitts and Nevis
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">
        Antigua
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_(island)" title="Saint Vincent (island)">
        St. Vincent
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Montserrat" title="Montserrat">
        Montserrat
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tortola" title="Tortola">
        Tortola
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint Croix, U.S. Virgin Islands">
        St. Croix
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Thomas,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="St. Thomas, U.S. Virgin Islands">
        St. Thomas
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">
        Guadeloupe
       </a>
       . They worked on sugarcane plantations and docks and settled mainly in the cities of
       <a href="/wiki/San_Pedro_de_Macor%C3%ADs" title="San Pedro de Macorís">
        San Pedro de Macorís
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Plata_(city)" title="Puerto Plata (city)">
        Puerto Plata
       </a>
       . Puerto Rican, and to a lesser extent, Cuban immigrants fled to the Dominican Republic from the mid-1800s until about 1940 due to a poor economy and social unrest in their respective home countries. Many Puerto Rican immigrants settled in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hig%C3%BCey_(city)" title="Higüey (city)">
        Higüey
       </a>
       , among other cities, and quickly assimilated due to similar culture. Before and during World War II, 800 Jewish refugees moved to the Dominican Republic.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SosuaJewishStudies_129-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-SosuaJewishStudies-129">
         [129]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Haitian_immigration">
        Haitian immigration
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Haitians_in_the_Dominican_Republic" title="Haitians in the Dominican Republic">
        Haitians in the Dominican Republic
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haiti_deforestation.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Haiti_deforestation.jpg/300px-Haiti_deforestation.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Haiti_deforestation.jpg/450px-Haiti_deforestation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Haiti_deforestation.jpg/600px-Haiti_deforestation.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Haiti_deforestation.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A satellite image of the border between the denuded landscape of
         <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">
          Haiti
         </a>
         (left) and the Dominican Republic (right), highlighting the
         <a href="/wiki/Deforestation_in_Haiti" title="Deforestation in Haiti">
          deforestation on the Haitian side
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dominicans_and_Haitians_Braving_the_Weather.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="427" data-file-width="640" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Dominicans_and_Haitians_Braving_the_Weather.jpg/300px-Dominicans_and_Haitians_Braving_the_Weather.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Dominicans_and_Haitians_Braving_the_Weather.jpg/450px-Dominicans_and_Haitians_Braving_the_Weather.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Dominicans_and_Haitians_Braving_the_Weather.jpg/600px-Dominicans_and_Haitians_Braving_the_Weather.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dominicans_and_Haitians_Braving_the_Weather.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Dominicans and Haitians lined up to attend medical providers from the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Army_Reserve" title="U.S. Army Reserve">
          U.S. Army Reserve
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Haiti is the neighboring nation to the Dominican Republic and is considerably poorer, less developed and is additionally the least developed country in the western hemisphere. In 2003, 80% of all Haitians were poor (54% living in abject poverty) and 47.1% were illiterate. The country of nine million people also has a fast growing population, but over two-thirds of the labor force lack formal jobs. Haiti's per capita GDP (PPP) was $1,300 in 2008, or less than one-sixth of the Dominican figure.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIADemo_6-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIADemo-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">
        <a href="#cite_note-159">
         [159]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As a result, hundreds of thousands of Haitians have migrated to the Dominican Republic, with some estimates of 800,000 Haitians in the country,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pinadep_102-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-pinadep-102">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
       while others put the Haitian-born population as high as one million.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">
        <a href="#cite_note-160">
         [160]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They usually work at low-paying and unskilled jobs in building construction and house cleaning and in sugar plantations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ferguson_161-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ferguson-161">
         [161]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There have been accusations that some Haitian immigrants work in slavery-like conditions and are severely exploited.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">
        <a href="#cite_note-162">
         [162]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Due to the lack of basic amenities and medical facilities in Haiti a large number of Haitian women, often arriving with several health problems, cross the border to Dominican soil. They deliberately come during their last weeks of pregnancy to obtain medical attention for childbirth, since Dominican public hospitals do not refuse medical services based on nationality or legal status. Statistics from a hospital in Santo Domingo report that over 22% of childbirths are by Haitian mothers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LD2008-01-21_163-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-LD2008-01-21-163">
         [163]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Haiti also
       <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_Haiti" title="Environmental issues in Haiti">
        suffers from severe environmental degradation
       </a>
       . Deforestation is rampant in Haiti; today less than 4 percent of Haiti's forests remain, and in many places the soil has eroded right down to the bedrock.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">
        <a href="#cite_note-164">
         [164]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Haitians burn wood charcoal for 60% of their domestic energy production. Because of Haiti running out of plant material to burn, Haitians have created an illegal market for coal on the Dominican side. Conservative estimates calculate the illegal movement of 115 tons of charcoal per week from the Dominican Republic to Haiti. Dominican officials estimate that at least 10 trucks per week are crossing the border loaded with charcoal.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165">
        <a href="#cite_note-165">
         [165]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2005, Dominican President Leonel Fernández criticized collective expulsions of Haitians as having taken place "in an abusive and inhuman way."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">
        <a href="#cite_note-166">
         [166]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After a UN delegation issued a preliminary report stating that it found a profound problem of racism and discrimination against people of Haitian origin, Dominican
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foreign_Minister" title="Foreign Minister">
        Foreign Minister
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Morales_Troncoso" title="Carlos Morales Troncoso">
        Carlos Morales Troncoso
       </a>
       issued a formal statement denouncing it, asserting that "our border with Haiti has its problems[;] this is our reality and it must be understood. It is important not to confuse national sovereignty with indifference, and not to confuse security with
       <a href="/wiki/Xenophobia" title="Xenophobia">
        xenophobia
       </a>
       ."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167">
        <a href="#cite_note-167">
         [167]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Children of Haitian immigrants are often
       <a href="/wiki/Statelessness" title="Statelessness">
        stateless
       </a>
       and denied services,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Vagueness" title="Wikipedia:Vagueness">
          <span title="This information is too vague. (November 2014)">
           vague
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       as their parents are denied Dominican nationality, being deemed transient residents due to their illegal or undocumented status; the children, though often eligible for Haitian nationality,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">
        <a href="#cite_note-168">
         [168]
        </a>
       </sup>
       are denied it by Haiti because of a lack of proper documents or witnesses.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169">
        <a href="#cite_note-169">
         [169]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170">
        <a href="#cite_note-170">
         [170]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171">
        <a href="#cite_note-171">
         [171]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172">
        <a href="#cite_note-172">
         [172]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Emigration">
        Emigration
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dominican_people_at_Dominican_parade,_New_York_City.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1784" data-file-width="2048" height="244" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Dominican_people_at_Dominican_parade%2C_New_York_City.jpg/280px-Dominican_people_at_Dominican_parade%2C_New_York_City.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Dominican_people_at_Dominican_parade%2C_New_York_City.jpg/420px-Dominican_people_at_Dominican_parade%2C_New_York_City.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Dominican_people_at_Dominican_parade%2C_New_York_City.jpg/560px-Dominican_people_at_Dominican_parade%2C_New_York_City.jpg 2x" width="280"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dominican_people_at_Dominican_parade,_New_York_City.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Day_Parade" title="Dominican Day Parade">
          Dominican Day Parade
         </a>
         in New York City, 2014
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominican_American" title="Dominican American">
        Dominican American
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic_immigration_to_Puerto_Rico" title="Dominican Republic immigration to Puerto Rico">
        Dominican Republic immigration to Puerto Rico
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The first of three late-20th century emigration waves began in 1961 after the assassination of dictator Trujillo,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wilderotter_173-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Wilderotter-173">
         [173]
        </a>
       </sup>
       due to fear of retaliation by Trujillo's allies and political uncertainty in general. In 1965 the United States began a military occupation of the Dominican Republic to end a civil war. Upon this, the U.S. eased travel restrictions, making it easier for Dominicans to obtain U.S. visas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174">
        <a href="#cite_note-174">
         [174]
        </a>
       </sup>
       From 1966 to 1978, the exodus continued, fueled by high unemployment and political repression. Communities established by the first wave of immigrants to the U.S. created a network that assisted subsequent arrivals.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Annenberg_Foundation_175-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Annenberg_Foundation-175">
         [175]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the early 1980s, underemployment, inflation, and the rise in value of the dollar all contributed to a third wave of emigration from the Dominican Republic. Today, emigration from the Dominican Republic remains high.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Annenberg_Foundation_175-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Annenberg_Foundation-175">
         [175]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2012 there were approximately 1.7 million people of Dominican descent in the U.S., counting both native- and foreign-born.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176">
        <a href="#cite_note-176">
         [176]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There was also a growing
       <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic_immigration_to_Puerto_Rico" title="Dominican Republic immigration to Puerto Rico">
        Dominican immigration to Puerto Rico
       </a>
       , with nearly 70,000 Dominicans living there as of 2010
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dominican_Republic&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       . Although that number is slowly decreasing and immigration trends have reversed because of Puerto Rico's economic crisis as of 2016.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Health">
        Health
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In 2007 the Dominican Republic had a
       <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">
        birth rate
       </a>
       of 22.91 per 1000 and a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Death_rate" title="Death rate">
        death rate
       </a>
       of 5.32 per 1000.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIADemo_6-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIADemo-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Youth_in_the_Dominican_Republic" title="Youth in the Dominican Republic">
        Youth in the Dominican Republic
       </a>
       is the healthiest age group.
      </p>
      <p>
       The prevalence of
       <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_the_Dominican_Republic" title="HIV/AIDS in the Dominican Republic">
        HIV/AIDS in the Dominican Republic
       </a>
       in 2011 stood at approximately 0.7%, which is relatively low by Caribbean standards, with an estimated 62,000 HIV/AIDS-positive Dominicans.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177">
        <a href="#cite_note-177">
         [177]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In contrast neighboring Haiti has an
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_HIV/AIDS_adult_prevalence_rate" title="List of countries by HIV/AIDS adult prevalence rate">
        HIV/AIDS rate more than double that of the Dominican Republic
       </a>
       . A mission based in the United States has been helping to combat AIDS in the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178">
        <a href="#cite_note-178">
         [178]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Dengue_fever" title="Dengue fever">
        Dengue fever
       </a>
       has become endemic to the republic, cases of malaria, and
       <a href="/wiki/Zika_virus" title="Zika virus">
        Zika virus
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179">
        <a href="#cite_note-179">
         [179]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180">
        <a href="#cite_note-180">
         [180]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The practice of abortion is illegal in all cases in the Dominican Republic, a ban that includes conceptions following rape, incest, and situations where the health of the mother is in danger, even if life-threatening.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181">
        <a href="#cite_note-181">
         [181]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This ban was reiterated by the Dominican government in a September 2009 provision of a constitutional reform bill.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182">
        <a href="#cite_note-182">
         [182]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_Dominican_Republic" title="Education in the Dominican Republic">
        Education in the Dominican Republic
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dominican_kids_in_Santo_Domingo.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Dominican_kids_in_Santo_Domingo.jpg/220px-Dominican_kids_in_Santo_Domingo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Dominican_kids_in_Santo_Domingo.jpg/330px-Dominican_kids_in_Santo_Domingo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Dominican_kids_in_Santo_Domingo.jpg/440px-Dominican_kids_in_Santo_Domingo.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dominican_kids_in_Santo_Domingo.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Kids taking classes
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Primary education is regulated by the Ministry of Education, with education being a right of all citizens and
       <a href="/wiki/Youth_in_the_Dominican_Republic" title="Youth in the Dominican Republic">
        youth in the Dominican Republic
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183">
        <a href="#cite_note-183">
         [183]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Preschool education is organized in different cycles and serves the 2–4 age group and the 4–6 age group. Preschool education is not mandatory except for the last year. Basic education is compulsory and serves the population of the 6–14 age group. Secondary education is not compulsory, although it is the duty of the state to offer it for free. It caters to the 14–18 age group and is organized in a common core of four years and three modes of two years of study that are offered in three different options: general or academic, vocational (industrial, agricultural, and services), and artistic.
      </p>
      <p>
       The higher education system consists of institutes and universities. The institutes offer courses of a higher technical level. The universities offer technical careers, undergraduate and graduate; these are regulated by the Ministry of Higher Education, Science and Technology.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184">
        <a href="#cite_note-184">
         [184]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">
        Crime
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_the_Dominican_Republic" title="Crime in the Dominican Republic">
        Crime in the Dominican Republic
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 2012 the Dominican Republic had a
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_intentional_homicide_rate" title="List of countries by intentional homicide rate">
        murder rate
       </a>
       of 22.1 per 100,000 population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNODC_185-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-UNODC-185">
         [185]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There was a total of 2,268 murders in the Dominican Republic in 2012.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNODC_185-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-UNODC-185">
         [185]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Dominican Republic has become a trans-shipment point for Colombian drugs destined for Europe as well as the United States and Canada.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIADemo_6-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIADemo-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_186-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-186">
         [186]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Money-laundering via the Dominican Republic is favored by Colombian drug cartels for the ease of illicit financial transactions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIADemo_6-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIADemo-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2004 it was estimated that 8% of all cocaine smuggled into the United States had come through the Dominican Republic.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187">
        <a href="#cite_note-187">
         [187]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Dominican Republic responded with increased efforts to seize drug shipments, arrest and extradite those involved, and combat money-laundering.
      </p>
      <p>
       The often light treatment of violent criminals has been a continuous source of local controversy. In April 2010, five teenagers, aged 15 to 17, shot and killed two taxi drivers and killed another five by forcing them to drink drain-cleaning acid. On September 24, 2010, the teens were sentenced to prison terms of three to five years, despite the protests of the taxi drivers' families.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188">
        <a href="#cite_note-188">
         [188]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_Dominican_Republic" title="Culture of the Dominican Republic">
        Culture of the Dominican Republic
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yoryi_Morel_02.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="356" data-file-width="320" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Yoryi_Morel_02.jpg/200px-Yoryi_Morel_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Yoryi_Morel_02.jpg/300px-Yoryi_Morel_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/0/03/Yoryi_Morel_02.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yoryi_Morel_02.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Campesino cibaeño, 1941 (Museo de Arte Moderno, Santo Domingo)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Culture and customs of the Dominican people have a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_culture" title="European culture">
        European cultural basis
       </a>
       , influenced by both
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_culture" title="African culture">
        African
       </a>
       and native
       <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">
        Taíno
       </a>
       elements;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EstevaFabregat_189-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-EstevaFabregat-189">
         [189]
        </a>
       </sup>
       culturally the Dominican Republic is among the most-European countries in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_America" title="Spanish America">
        Spanish America
       </a>
       , alongside
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Culture of Puerto Rico">
        Puerto Rico
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Cuba" title="Culture of Cuba">
        Cuba
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Chile" title="Central Chile">
        Central Chile
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Argentina" title="Culture of Argentina">
        Argentina
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Uruguay" title="Culture of Uruguay">
        Uruguay
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EstevaFabregat_189-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-EstevaFabregat-189">
         [189]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       European, African, and Taíno cultural elements are evident in cuisine, architecture, language, family structure, religion, and music.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">
        Architecture
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The architecture in the Dominican Republic represents a complex blend of diverse cultures. The deep influence of the
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        European
       </a>
       colonists is the most evident throughout the country. Characterized by ornate designs and
       <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">
        baroque
       </a>
       structures, the style can best be seen in the capital city of
       <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">
        Santo Domingo
       </a>
       , which is home to the first cathedral, castle, monastery, and fortress in all of the
       <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">
        Americas
       </a>
       , located in the city's
       <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_Colonial_(Santo_Domingo)" title="Ciudad Colonial (Santo Domingo)">
        Colonial Zone
       </a>
       , an area declared as a
       <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">
        World Heritage Site
       </a>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
        UNESCO
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190">
        <a href="#cite_note-190">
         [190]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191">
        <a href="#cite_note-191">
         [191]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The designs carry over into the villas and buildings throughout the country. It can also be observed on buildings that contain stucco exteriors, arched doors and windows, and red tiled roofs.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USMC,_1922,_Santo_Domingo,_Dominican_Republic_20_of_26_(6227519514).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="958" data-file-width="1651" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/USMC%2C_1922%2C_Santo_Domingo%2C_Dominican_Republic_20_of_26_%286227519514%29.jpg/250px-USMC%2C_1922%2C_Santo_Domingo%2C_Dominican_Republic_20_of_26_%286227519514%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/USMC%2C_1922%2C_Santo_Domingo%2C_Dominican_Republic_20_of_26_%286227519514%29.jpg/375px-USMC%2C_1922%2C_Santo_Domingo%2C_Dominican_Republic_20_of_26_%286227519514%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/USMC%2C_1922%2C_Santo_Domingo%2C_Dominican_Republic_20_of_26_%286227519514%29.jpg/500px-USMC%2C_1922%2C_Santo_Domingo%2C_Dominican_Republic_20_of_26_%286227519514%29.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USMC,_1922,_Santo_Domingo,_Dominican_Republic_20_of_26_(6227519514).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A
         <i>
          bohío
         </i>
         near Santo Domingo, 1922. Most Dominicans, particularly those in rural areas, used to live in
         <i>
          bohíos
         </i>
         until well into the mid-20th century, like the native
         <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">
          Taínos
         </a>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cordero_192-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-Cordero-192">
           [192]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The indigenous peoples of the Dominican Republic have also had a significant influence on the architecture of the country. The
       <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">
        Taíno
       </a>
       people relied heavily on the mahogany and guano (dried palm tree leaf) to put together crafts, artwork, furniture, and houses. Utilizing mud, thatched roofs, and mahogany trees, they gave buildings and the furniture inside a natural look, seamlessly blending in with the island’s surroundings.
      </p>
      <p>
       Lately, with the rise in tourism and increasing popularity as a Caribbean vacation destination, architects in the Dominican Republic have now begun to incorporate cutting-edge designs that emphasize luxury. In many ways an architectural playground, villas and hotels implement new styles, while offering new takes on the old. This new style is characterized by simplified, angular corners and large windows that blend outdoor and indoor spaces. As with the culture as a whole, contemporary architects embrace the Dominican Republic's rich history and various cultures to create something new. Surveying modern villas, one can find any combination of the three major styles: a villa may contain angular, modernist building construction, Spanish Colonial-style arched windows, and a traditional Taino hammock in the bedroom balcony.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">
        Cuisine
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           does not
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
            cite
           </a>
           any
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            sources
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dominican_Republic&amp;action=edit">

           </a>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">

           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">

          </span>
