       </tr>
      </table>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_the_Dominican_Republic" title="Cuisine of the Dominican Republic">
        Cuisine of the Dominican Republic
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ChicharronMixto.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/ChicharronMixto.JPG/220px-ChicharronMixto.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/ChicharronMixto.JPG/330px-ChicharronMixto.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/ChicharronMixto.JPG/440px-ChicharronMixto.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ChicharronMixto.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Chicharrón mixto
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Dominican cuisine is predominantly
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_cuisine#Spanish_regional_variation:_typical_dishes_and_meal_routines" title="Spanish cuisine">
        Spanish
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno#Food_and_agriculture" title="Taíno">
        Taíno
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/African_cuisine" title="African cuisine">
        African
       </a>
       . The typical cuisine is quite similar to what can be found in other Latin American countries, but many of the names of dishes are different. One breakfast dish consists of eggs and
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mang%C3%BA_(dish)" title="Mangú (dish)">
         mangú
        </a>
       </i>
       (mashed, boiled plantain). Heartier versions of
       <i>
        mangú
       </i>
       are accompanied by deep-fried meat (Dominican salami, typically), cheese, or both. Lunch, generally the largest and most important meal of the day, usually consists of rice, meat, beans, and salad. "La Bandera" (literally "The Flag") is the most popular lunch dish; it consists of meat and red beans on white rice.
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Sancocho" title="Sancocho">
         Sancocho
        </a>
       </i>
       is a stew often made with seven varieties of meat.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Patacones.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Patacones.JPG/200px-Patacones.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Patacones.JPG/300px-Patacones.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Patacones.JPG/400px-Patacones.JPG 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Patacones.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Tostones, a fried plantain dish
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Meals tend to favor meats and starches over dairy products and vegetables. Many dishes are made with
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Sofrito" title="Sofrito">
         sofrito
        </a>
       </i>
       , which is a mix of local herbs used as a wet rub for meats and sautéed to bring out all of a dish's flavors. Throughout the south-central coast,
       <a href="/wiki/Bulgur" title="Bulgur">
        bulgur
       </a>
       , or whole wheat, is a main ingredient in
       <a href="/wiki/Tabbouleh" title="Tabbouleh">
        <i>
         quipes
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         tipili
        </i>
       </a>
       (bulgur salad). Other favorite Dominican foods include
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Chicharr%C3%B3n" title="Chicharrón">
         chicharrón
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">
         yuca
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Tapioca" title="Tapioca">
         casabe
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Cuban_pastry" title="Cuban pastry">
         pastelitos
        </a>
       </i>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Empanada" title="Empanada">
        empanadas
       </a>
       ),
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potato" title="Sweet potato">
         batata
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">
        yam
       </a>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Pasteles" title="Pasteles">
         pasteles en hoja
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Chimichurris" title="Chimichurris">
         chimichurris
        </a>
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Tostones" title="Tostones">
         tostones
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Some treats Dominicans enjoy are
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Rice_pudding" title="Rice pudding">
         arroz con leche
        </a>
       </i>
       (or
       <i>
        arroz con dulce
       </i>
       ),
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Bizcocho_Dominicano" title="Bizcocho Dominicano">
         bizcocho dominicano
        </a>
       </i>
       (lit. Dominican cake),
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Habichuelas_con_dulce" title="Habichuelas con dulce">
         habichuelas con dulce
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Flan" title="Flan">
        flan
       </a>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Snow_cone" title="Snow cone">
         frío frío
        </a>
       </i>
       (snow cones),
       <a href="/wiki/Dulce_de_leche" title="Dulce de leche">
        dulce de leche
       </a>
       , and
       <i>
        caña
       </i>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">
        sugarcane
       </a>
       ). The beverages Dominicans enjoy are
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Morir_So%C3%B1ando" title="Morir Soñando">
         Morir Soñando
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rum" title="Rum">
        rum
       </a>
       , beer,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Mama_Juana" title="Mama Juana">
         Mama Juana
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193">
        <a href="#cite_note-193">
         [193]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <i>
        batida
       </i>
       (smoothie), jugos naturales (freshly squeezed fruit juices),
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Mauby" title="Mauby">
         mabí
        </a>
       </i>
       , coffee, and
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Chaca_(dessert)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Chaca (dessert) (page does not exist)">
         chaca
        </a>
       </i>
       (also called
       <i>
        maiz caqueao/casqueado
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        maiz con dulce
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        maiz con leche
       </i>
       ), the last item being found only in the southern provinces of the country such as San Juan.
      </p>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_dance">
        Music and dance
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_Dominican_Republic" title="Music of the Dominican Republic">
        Music of the Dominican Republic
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Merengue_dancing.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3743" data-file-width="2495" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Merengue_dancing.jpg/150px-Merengue_dancing.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Merengue_dancing.jpg/225px-Merengue_dancing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Merengue_dancing.jpg/300px-Merengue_dancing.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Merengue_dancing.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Merengue music
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Musically, the Dominican Republic is known for the
       <a href="/wiki/Popular_culture" title="Popular culture">
        world popular
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Musical_style" title="Musical style">
        musical style
       </a>
       and genre called
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Merengue_music" title="Merengue music">
         merengue
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harvey2006_194-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Harvey2006-194">
         [194]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         376–7
        </span>
       </sup>
       a type of lively, fast-paced rhythm and dance music consisting of a tempo of about 120 to 160 beats per minute (though it varies) based on musical elements like drums, brass, chorded instruments, and accordion, as well as some elements unique to the Spanish-speaking Caribbean, such as the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Tambora_(Dominican_drum)" title="Tambora (Dominican drum)">
         tambora
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/G%C3%BCira" title="Güira">
         güira
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Its
       <a href="/wiki/Syncopation" title="Syncopation">
        syncopated beats
       </a>
       use
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_percussion" title="Latin percussion">
        Latin percussion
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brass_instruments" title="Brass instruments">
        brass instruments
       </a>
       , bass, and piano or keyboard. Between 1937 and 1950 merengue music was promoted internationally by Dominican groups like Billo's Caracas Boys, Chapuseaux and Damiron "Los Reyes del Merengue," Joseito Mateo, and others. Radio, television, and international media popularized it further. Some well known merengue performers are
       <a href="/wiki/Wilfrido_Vargas" title="Wilfrido Vargas">
        Wilfrido Vargas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Ventura" title="Johnny Ventura">
        Johnny Ventura
       </a>
       , singer-songwriter
       <a href="/wiki/Los_Hermanos_Rosario" title="Los Hermanos Rosario">
        Los Hermanos Rosario
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Luis_Guerra" title="Juan Luis Guerra">
        Juan Luis Guerra
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Villalona" title="Fernando Villalona">
        Fernando Villalona
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eddy_Herrera" title="Eddy Herrera">
        Eddy Herrera
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Vargas" title="Sergio Vargas">
        Sergio Vargas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/To%C3%B1o_Rosario" title="Toño Rosario">
        Toño Rosario
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Milly_Quezada" title="Milly Quezada">
        Milly Quezada
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Chich%C3%AD_Peralta" title="Chichí Peralta">
        Chichí Peralta
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Merengue became popular in the United States, mostly on the
       <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">
        East Coast
       </a>
       , during the 1980s and 1990s,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harvey2006_194-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Harvey2006-194">
         [194]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         375
        </span>
       </sup>
       when many Dominican artists residing in the U.S. (particularly New York) started performing in the Latin club scene and gained radio airplay. They included Victor Roque y La Gran Manzana, Henry Hierro, Zacarias Ferreira, Aventura, and Milly Jocelyn Y Los Vecinos. The emergence of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Bachata_(music)" title="Bachata (music)">
         bachata
        </a>
       </i>
       , along with an increase in the number of Dominicans living among other
       <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">
        Latino
       </a>
       groups in New York,
       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">
        New Jersey
       </a>
       , and Florida, has contributed to Dominican music's overall growth in popularity.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harvey2006_194-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Harvey2006-194">
         [194]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         378
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Juan_Luis_Guerra_en_Acceso_Total_(6).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="360" data-file-width="640" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Juan_Luis_Guerra_en_Acceso_Total_%286%29.jpg/220px-Juan_Luis_Guerra_en_Acceso_Total_%286%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Juan_Luis_Guerra_en_Acceso_Total_%286%29.jpg/330px-Juan_Luis_Guerra_en_Acceso_Total_%286%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Juan_Luis_Guerra_en_Acceso_Total_%286%29.jpg/440px-Juan_Luis_Guerra_en_Acceso_Total_%286%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Juan_Luis_Guerra_en_Acceso_Total_(6).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Dominican singer
         <a href="/wiki/Juan_Luis_Guerra" title="Juan Luis Guerra">
          Juan Luis Guerra
         </a>
         in concert, 2010
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Bachata_(music)" title="Bachata (music)">
        Bachata
       </a>
       , a form of music and dance that originated in the countryside and rural marginal neighborhoods of the Dominican Republic, has become quite popular in recent years. Its subjects are often romantic; especially prevalent are tales of heartbreak and sadness. In fact, the original name for the genre was
       <i>
        amargue
       </i>
       ("bitterness," or "bitter music," or blues music), until the rather ambiguous (and mood-neutral) term
       <i>
        bachata
       </i>
       became popular. Bachata grew out of, and is still closely related to, the
       <a href="/wiki/Pan-Latinism" title="Pan-Latinism">
        pan-Latin
       </a>
       American romantic style called
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Bolero" title="Bolero">
         bolero
        </a>
       </i>
       . Over time, it has been influenced by merengue and by a variety of Latin American guitar styles.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Palo_music" title="Palo music">
        Palo
       </a>
       is an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-Dominican_(Dominican_Republic)" title="Afro-Dominican (Dominican Republic)">
        Afro-Dominican
       </a>
       sacred music that can be found throughout the island. The drum and human voice are the principal instruments. Palo is played at religious ceremonies—usually coinciding with saints' religious feast days—as well as for secular parties and special occasions. Its roots are in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congo_region" title="Congo region">
        Congo region
       </a>
       of central-west Africa, but it is mixed with European influences in the melodies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195">
        <a href="#cite_note-195">
         [195]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Salsa_music" title="Salsa music">
        Salsa music
       </a>
       has had a great deal of popularity in the country. During the late 1960s Dominican musicians like
       <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Pacheco" title="Johnny Pacheco">
        Johnny Pacheco
       </a>
       , creator of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fania_All_Stars" title="Fania All Stars">
        Fania All Stars
       </a>
       , played a significant role in the development and popularization of the genre.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Dominican_rock" title="Dominican rock">
        Dominican rock
       </a>
       is also popular. Many, if not the majority, of its performers are based in Santo Domingo and Santiago.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fashion">
        Fashion
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oscar_de_la_Renta_by_foto_di_matti.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="351" data-file-width="250" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Oscar_de_la_Renta_by_foto_di_matti.jpg/150px-Oscar_de_la_Renta_by_foto_di_matti.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Oscar_de_la_Renta_by_foto_di_matti.jpg/225px-Oscar_de_la_Renta_by_foto_di_matti.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/03/Oscar_de_la_Renta_by_foto_di_matti.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Oscar_de_la_Renta_by_foto_di_matti.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Dominican native, fashion designer and perfume maker
         <a href="/wiki/Oscar_de_la_Renta" title="Oscar de la Renta">
          Oscar de la Renta
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The country boasts one of the ten most important design schools in the region, La Escuela de Diseño de Altos de Chavón, which is making the country a key player in the world of fashion and design. Noted fashion designer
       <a href="/wiki/Oscar_de_la_Renta" title="Oscar de la Renta">
        Oscar de la Renta
       </a>
       was born in the Dominican Republic in 1932, and became a US citizen in 1971. He studied under the leading Spaniard designer
       <a href="/wiki/Crist%C3%B3bal_Balenciaga" title="Cristóbal Balenciaga">
        Cristóbal Balenciaga
       </a>
       and then worked with the house of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lanvin_(clothing)" title="Lanvin (clothing)">
        Lanvin
       </a>
       in Paris. By 1963, he had designs bearing his own label. After establishing himself in the US, de la Renta opened boutiques across the country.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (September 2017)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       His work blends French and Spaniard fashion with American styles.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196">
        <a href="#cite_note-196">
         [196]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica_de_la_renta_197-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-britannica_de_la_renta-197">
         [197]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Although he settled in New York, de la Renta also marketed his work in Latin America, where it became very popular, and remained active in his native Dominican Republic, where his charitable activities and personal achievements earned him the Juan Pablo Duarte Order of Merit and the Order of Cristóbal Colón.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica_de_la_renta_197-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-britannica_de_la_renta-197">
         [197]
        </a>
       </sup>
       De la Renta died of complications from cancer on October 20, 2014.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="National_symbols">
        National symbols
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pereskia_quisqueyana.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="1412" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Pereskia_quisqueyana.JPG/150px-Pereskia_quisqueyana.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Pereskia_quisqueyana.JPG/225px-Pereskia_quisqueyana.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Pereskia_quisqueyana.JPG/300px-Pereskia_quisqueyana.JPG 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pereskia_quisqueyana.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Bayahibe Rose
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Some of the Dominican Republic's important symbols are the
       <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_Dominican_Republic" title="Flag of the Dominican Republic">
        flag
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_the_Dominican_Republic" title="Coat of arms of the Dominican Republic">
        the coat of arms
       </a>
       , and the national anthem, titled
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/National_Anthem_of_the_Dominican_Republic" title="National Anthem of the Dominican Republic">
         Himno Nacional
        </a>
       </i>
       . The flag has a large white cross that divides it into four quarters. Two quarters are red and two are blue. Red represents the blood shed by the liberators. Blue expresses God's protection over the nation. The white cross symbolizes the struggle of the liberators to bequeath future generations a free nation. An alternate interpretation is that blue represents the ideals of progress and liberty, whereas white symbolizes peace and unity among Dominicans.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198">
        <a href="#cite_note-198">
         [198]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the center of the cross is the Dominican coat of arms, in the same colors as the national flag. The coat of arms pictures a red, white, and blue flag-draped shield with a Bible, a gold cross, and arrows; the shield is surrounded by an olive branch (on the left) and a palm branch (on the right). The Bible traditionally represents the truth and the light. The gold cross symbolizes the redemption from slavery, and the arrows symbolize the noble soldiers and their proud military. A blue ribbon above the shield reads, "Dios, Patria, Libertad" (meaning "God, Fatherland, Liberty"). A red ribbon under the shield reads, "República Dominicana" (meaning "Dominican Republic"). Out of all the flags in the world, the depiction of a Bible is unique to the Dominican flag.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Floral_emblem" title="Floral emblem">
        national flower
       </a>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/Pereskia_quisqueyana" title="Pereskia quisqueyana">
        Bayahibe Rose
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_tree" title="National tree">
        national tree
       </a>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/Swietenia_mahagoni" title="Swietenia mahagoni">
        West Indian Mahogany
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199">
        <a href="#cite_note-199">
         [199]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The national bird is the
       <i>
        Cigua Palmera
       </i>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Palmchat" title="Palmchat">
        Palmchat
       </a>
       ("Dulus dominicus").
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-depaul_200-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-depaul-200">
         [200]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Dominican Republic celebrates
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dia_de_la_Altagracia" title="Dia de la Altagracia">
        Dia de la Altagracia
       </a>
       on January 21 in honor of its patroness,
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Pablo_Duarte" title="Juan Pablo Duarte">
        Duarte
       </a>
       's Day on January 26 in honor of one of its founding fathers, Independence Day on February 27,
       <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Restoration_War" title="Dominican Restoration War">
        Restoration Day
       </a>
       on August 16,
       <i>
        Virgen de las Mercedes
       </i>
       on September 24, and
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_Day" title="Constitution Day">
        Constitution Day
       </a>
       on November 6.
      </p>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
        Sports
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sports_in_the_Dominican_Republic" title="Sports in the Dominican Republic">
        Sports in the Dominican Republic
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DSC00621_Albert_Pujols.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3100" data-file-width="1550" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/DSC00621_Albert_Pujols.jpg/100px-DSC00621_Albert_Pujols.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/DSC00621_Albert_Pujols.jpg/150px-DSC00621_Albert_Pujols.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/DSC00621_Albert_Pujols.jpg/200px-DSC00621_Albert_Pujols.jpg 2x" width="100"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DSC00621_Albert_Pujols.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Dominican native and
         <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">
          Major League Baseball
         </a>
         player
         <a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">
          Albert Pujols
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">
        Baseball
       </a>
       is by far the most popular sport in the Dominican Republic.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harvey2006_194-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Harvey2006-194">
         [194]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         59
        </span>
       </sup>
       The country has a baseball league of six teams. Its season usually begins in October and ends in January. After the United States, the Dominican Republic has the second highest number of
       <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">
        Major League Baseball
       </a>
       (MLB) players.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ozzie_Virgil,_Sr." title="Ozzie Virgil, Sr.">
        Ozzie Virgil, Sr.
       </a>
       became the first Dominican-born player in the MLB on September 23, 1956.
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Marichal" title="Juan Marichal">
        Juan Marichal
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Mart%C3%ADnez" title="Pedro Martínez">
        Pedro Martínez
       </a>
       are the only Dominican-born players in the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum">
        Baseball Hall of Fame
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201">
        <a href="#cite_note-201">
         [201]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other notable baseball players born in the Dominican Republic are
       <a href="/wiki/Adri%C3%A1n_Beltr%C3%A9" title="Adrián Beltré">
        Adrián Beltré
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Robinson_Can%C3%B3" title="Robinson Canó">
        Robinson Canó
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rico_Carty" title="Rico Carty">
        Rico Carty
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Starling_Marte" title="Starling Marte">
        Starling Marte
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Guerrero" title="Vladimir Guerrero">
        Vladimir Guerrero
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/George_Bell_(outfielder)" title="George Bell (outfielder)">
        George Bell
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Julian_Javier" title="Julian Javier">
        Julian Javier
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Liriano" title="Francisco Liriano">
        Francisco Liriano
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manny_Ram%C3%ADrez" title="Manny Ramírez">
        Manny Ramírez
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Bautista" title="José Bautista">
        José Bautista
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Encarnaci%C3%B3n" title="Edwin Encarnación">
        Edwin Encarnación
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hanley_Ram%C3%ADrez" title="Hanley Ramírez">
        Hanley Ramírez
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/David_Ortiz" title="David Ortiz">
        David Ortiz
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">
        Albert Pujols
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Cruz" title="Nelson Cruz">
        Nelson Cruz
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ubaldo_Jim%C3%A9nez" title="Ubaldo Jiménez">
        Ubaldo Jiménez
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Reyes_(shortstop)" title="José Reyes (shortstop)">
        José Reyes
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pl%C3%A1cido_Polanco" title="Plácido Polanco">
        Plácido Polanco
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Sammy_Sosa" title="Sammy Sosa">
        Sammy Sosa
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Felipe_Alou" title="Felipe Alou">
        Felipe Alou
       </a>
       has also enjoyed success as a manager
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202">
        <a href="#cite_note-202">
         [202]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Omar_Minaya" title="Omar Minaya">
        Omar Minaya
       </a>
       as a general manager. In 2013, the Dominican team went undefeated
       <i>
        en route
       </i>
       to winning the
       <a href="/wiki/2013_World_Baseball_Classic" title="2013 World Baseball Classic">
        World Baseball Classic
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">
        boxing
       </a>
       , the country has produced scores of world-class fighters and several world champions,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203">
        <a href="#cite_note-203">
         [203]
        </a>
       </sup>
       such as
       <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Cruz_(boxer)" title="Carlos Cruz (boxer)">
        Carlos Cruz
       </a>
       , his brother
       <a href="/wiki/Leo_Cruz" title="Leo Cruz">
        Leo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Guzman_(boxer)" title="Juan Guzman (boxer)">
        Juan Guzman
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joan_Guzman" title="Joan Guzman">
        Joan Guzman
       </a>
       . Basketball also enjoys a relatively high level of popularity.
       <a href="/wiki/Tito_Horford" title="Tito Horford">
        Tito Horford
       </a>
       , his son
       <a href="/wiki/Al_Horford" title="Al Horford">
        Al
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Felipe_L%C3%B3pez_(basketball)" title="Felipe López (basketball)">
        Felipe Lopez
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Garc%C3%ADa_(basketball)" title="Francisco García (basketball)">
        Francisco Garcia
       </a>
       are among the Dominican-born players currently or formerly in the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">
        National Basketball Association
       </a>
       (NBA). Olympic gold medalist and world champion hurdler
       <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_S%C3%A1nchez" title="Félix Sánchez">
        Félix Sánchez
       </a>
       hails from the Dominican Republic, as does
       <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">
        NFL
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Defensive_end" title="Defensive end">
        defensive end
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Luis_Castillo_(American_football)" title="Luis Castillo (American football)">
        Luis Castillo
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204">
        <a href="#cite_note-204">
         [204]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Other important sports are
       <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">
        volleyball
       </a>
       , introduced in 1916 by U.S. Marines and controlled by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominican_Volleyball_Federation" title="Dominican Volleyball Federation">
        Dominican Volleyball Federation
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Taekwondo" title="Taekwondo">
        taekwondo
       </a>
       , in which
       <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Mercedes" title="Gabriel Mercedes">
        Gabriel Mercedes
       </a>
       won an Olympic silver medal in 2008, and
       <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">
        judo
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205">
        <a href="#cite_note-205">
         [205]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>

         <span class="reference-text">
          <i>
           Terrenos comuneros
          </i>
          arose because of "scarce population, low value of the land, the absence of officials qualified to survey the lands, and the difficulty of dividing up the ranch in such a way that each would receive a share of the grasslands, forests, streams, palm groves, and small agricultural plots that, only when combined, made possible the exploitation of the ranch." (Hoetink,
          <i>
           The Dominican People: Notes for a Historical Sociology

        <li id="cite_note-Lebanon-migrants-register-158">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          ^
          <a href="#cite_ref-Lebanon-migrants-register_158-0">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              a
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-Lebanon-migrants-register_158-1">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              b
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation web">
           González Hernández, Julio Amable (August 11, 2012).
           <a class="external text" href="http://www.idg.org.do/capsulas/agosto2012/agosto201211.htm" rel="nofollow">
            "Registro de Inmigrantes de El Líbano"
           </a>
           .
           <i>
            Cápsulas Genealógicas en Areíto
           </i>
           (in Spanish). Santo Domingo: Instituto Dominicano de Genealogía
           <span class="reference-accessdate">
            . Retrieved
            <span class="nowrap">
             May 28,
            </span>
            2013
           </span>
           .
           <q>
            Recientemente conocimos un trabajo que se está llevando a cabo en el Club Libanés Sirio Palestino y que consiste en la elaboración de un minucioso registro de todos los inmigrantes que llegaron a la República Dominicana procedentes de El Líbano a fines del siglo XIX y principios del XX. (...) En menor grado, también se está recabando información de los inmigrantes procedentes de Siria y Palestina. Hasta el presente, ya se tienen registros de unos 600 libaneses, 200 palestinos y 200 sirios. (...) Se calcula que en República Dominicana existen unos 80,000 descendientes de esos inmigrantes que una vez dejaron sus tierras para buscar una vida mejor.
           </q>
          </cite>

           <q>
            ARTICLE 11: Any person born of a Haitian father or Haitian mother who are themselves native-born Haitians and have never renounced their nationality possesses Haitian nationality at the time of birth.
           </q>

          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=San+Diego+Hall+of+Champions+%E2%80%93+Sports+at+Lunch%2C+Luis+Castillo+and+Felix+Sanchez&amp;rft.pub=San+Diego+Hall+of+Champions&amp;rft.date=2007-03-24&amp;rft.aulast=Shanahan&amp;rft.aufirst=Tom&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.sdhoc.com%2Fmain%2Farticles%2Fsportsatlunch%2FSportsatlunch2007%2FSanchezcastillo&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ADominican+Republic">
           <span style="display:none;">

          </span>
         </span>
